  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dde6a748-b916-45f0-951f-e3854d9bd722'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13494975325859809464">In Murder Red Ink, Mord McGhee imaginatively explores the incomprehensible depths of horror, human nature, and captures the brutal reality of the monster behind the Jack the Ripper murders in 1888. Allena Gould moves among the horror brought into the future of Chicago where technological ghosts are a reality and historical interface programs can be rewritten and interacted</span>
  <span id="freeText13494975325859809464" style="display:none">In Murder Red Ink, Mord McGhee imaginatively explores the incomprehensible depths of horror, human nature, and captures the brutal reality of the monster behind the Jack the Ripper murders in 1888. Allena Gould moves among the horror brought into the future of Chicago where technological ghosts are a reality and historical interface programs can be rewritten and interacted with. Once a talented prodigy, she wrestles her way through incomprehensible nightmares. Torture and murder as seen through the eyes of the Ripper himself in a science fiction whirlwind of the darkest sort. McGhee's vision of apocalyptic dread is not for the passing reader, it's a literary odyssey of gore meant to be enjoyed by those who like to be terrifically disturbed. NY TIMES best-selling author of MEG &amp; THE LOCH notes, "Graphic. Intense. Provocative. The psychological thriller has a new voice and it is Mord McGhee."<br /><br />*2nd Edition includes foreword by Robert E. Anderson, Casebook.org senior forum and Jack the Ripper speaker.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13494975325859809464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1114577998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114577998" />
    <a title="Adam Crissom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37285292-adam-crissom"><img alt="Adam Crissom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425220677p2/37285292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114577998?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Crissom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Crissom" href="/user/show/37285292-adam-crissom">Adam Crissom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114577998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11900759059461470765">Saw the editorial on facebook and picked this up on kindle. I didn't realize it was new. This book blew my mind. I don't like scifi that much because it tends to drag on and only appeal to hardcore types. I like crime non-fiction and the connections made to the Ripper killings in London was a wicked and shocking twist. If you have bad dreams easily steer clear. If you like serial killer murder mysteries and tv shows like American Horror Story this is one hell of a thriller.<br/><br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5562028305575332861">Disclaimer: I received an e-copy in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>I personally loved "Ghosts of San Francisco" and I'm an avid reader of anything having to do with Jack the Ripper, so when I was given the opportunity to read and review "Murder Red Ink," there was no way I could pass it up.   <span id="freeText5562028305575332861" style="display:none">Disclaimer: I received an e-copy in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />I personally loved "Ghosts of San Francisco" and I'm an avid reader of anything having to do with Jack the Ripper, so when I was given the opportunity to read and review "Murder Red Ink," there was no way I could pass it up. And once again, Mr. McGhee does not disappoint!<br /><br />This book involves a very interesting take on the Ripper murders, and it kept me engrossed from beginning to end. There were many times I had to put it down because of that pesky thing called "life," but I just didn't want to, and that's how you know a book is awesome.<br /><br />Wonderful novel, tantalizing plot and theories, and another great story from this author. Keep 'em coming! =)<br /><br />5 stars</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jack the Ripper, Stephen King, Ray Bradbury, Alfred Hitchcock</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1126845128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3239214021901635078">I'm a fickle reader. I don't usually buy into the "sleepers" I see on goodreads. This one of the best new books I've read in years. If you like serial killer mysteries I suggest this book. Every once in a while somebody new comes along. My guess is this is a pen name from an author that is crossing genre. The book combines so many things and has so many layers going on that I am going to have to reread it (willingly!) All of it done with an unexpected and appreciated mastery <br/><br/> </span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7053778696789815396">I was a bit in two minds with this book (won in a giveaway); on the one hand I struggled to get into a non linear story with multiple strands, but maybe that was more me than the book, on the other hand it was a fresh treatment of a topic that's been done many times before, and that hand was dripping with blood from a very sharp blade! Read it and see for yourself.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299915253" />

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul W. Nielsen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul W. Nielsen" href="/user/show/23183730-paul-w-nielsen">Paul W. Nielsen</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299915253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3758453188557771074">Murder Red Ink is not for the reader who wants to curl up and relax. It is for the sophisticated Sci-fi reader who has a brain and wants to use it. Don't bother trying to get ahead of the author, you won't succeed. <br/>A couple of things really stand out with this author:<br/>1. He is a true wordsmith. By that,I don't mean he just uses a complete vocabulary, but is truly skilled with the use of words. He can take a complete paragraph and condense it to two or three words which gives a far better image th</span>
  <span id="freeText3758453188557771074" style="display:none">Murder Red Ink is not for the reader who wants to curl up and relax. It is for the sophisticated Sci-fi reader who has a brain and wants to use it. Don't bother trying to get ahead of the author, you won't succeed. <br />A couple of things really stand out with this author:<br />1. He is a true wordsmith. By that,I don't mean he just uses a complete vocabulary, but is truly skilled with the use of words. He can take a complete paragraph and condense it to two or three words which gives a far better image than the paragraph. That takes talent.<br />2. The insight he gives into a characters mind is amazing. He's either ill or talented and I suspect the latter (but I could be wrong). <br />If this is your genre, Murder Red Ink is a must read. <br /> </span>

  <span id="freeText18156265129174409817" style="display:none">Mixture of timelines with intrigue and some disturbing imagery.<br />While no actual people or theories are named it is an interesting take on the Jack the Ripper slayings in 1800s. You will not figure this one out ahead and it is not for the casual, light reader. This is an intense trip into the psychological terror of the ugliness of mankind, yet holding true to the persistency of hope.<br />When the big conclusion hit I was not sure what was going on but then bang an assembly line of monsters, tense violent scenes, and a fantastic birth of a powerful female lead. It felt as if a sequel was being set up but have not seen any mention of one. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qERdriOJNwZ6znlTpZ7gulzgDyGlNnEKjUAtmFUZIStqX6iqei4LY/vXV8wIwTbcMJzh+8qU6c4P8CDLgw9xQA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Bs6VwSMdtDAtrF6uWSy5cBQ6+59vFp2fl+sueCu6hMLE1WDFerqIVay1cDH0c28WeEYVRQC0BVsVWyMr/azUqQ==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_148775'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/148775.The_Day_the_World_Came_to_Town?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Day the World Came to Town: 9/11 in Gander, Newfoundland<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/86082.Jim_DeFede?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Jim DeFede<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.19 avg rating &mdash; 26,393 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2002\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer3332938842083087064\">Perfect for fans of the hit Broadway musical Come from Away.\nWhen 38 jetliners bound for the United States were forced to land at Gander International Airport in Canada by the closing of U.S. airspace on September 11, the population of this small tow<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3332938842083087064\" style=\"display:none\">Perfect for fans of the hit Broadway musical Come from Away.\nWhen 38 jetliners bound for the United States were forced to land at Gander International Airport in Canada by the closing of U.S. airspace on September 11, the population of this small town on Newfoundland Island swelled from 10,300 to nearly 17,000. The citizens of Gander met the stranded passengers with an overwhelming display of friendship and goodwill. As the passengers stepped from the airplanes, exhausted, hungry and distraught after being held on board for nearly 24 hours while security checked all of the baggage, they were greeted with a feast prepared by the townspeople. Local bus drivers who had been on strike came off the picket lines to transport the passengers to the various shelters set up in local schools and churches. Linens and toiletries were bought and donated. A middle school provided showers, as well as access to computers, email, and televisions, allowing the passengers to stay in touch with family and follow the news.\n\nOver the course of those four days, many of the passengers developed friendships with Gander residents that they expect to last a lifetime. As a show of thanks, scholarship funds for the children of Gander have been formed and donations have been made to provide new computers for the schools. This book recounts the inspiring story of the residents of Gander, Canada, whose acts of kindness have touched the lives of thousands of people and been an example of humanity and goodwill.<\/span>\n <span id="freeTextContainer1983232106725788649">"Intense. Graphic. Provocative. The psychological thriller has a new voice and it is Mord McGhee," said Steve Alten.<br/><br/>"Even if you hate reading, this book will change that. Pageturner, blew me away," said George C. Romero<br/><br/>"A uniquely intellectual American book," says Loren Coleman<br/><br/>"With the skill and aplomb of Philip K. Dick," says Robert E.   <span id="freeText1983232106725788649" style="display:none">"Intense. Graphic. Provocative. The psychological thriller has a new voice and it is Mord McGhee," said Steve Alten.<br /><br />"Even if you hate reading, this book will change that. Pageturner, blew me away," said George C. Romero<br /><br />"A uniquely intellectual American book," says Loren Coleman<br /><br />"With the skill and aplomb of Philip K. Dick," says Robert E. Anderson<br /><br />"A great addition to the genre," says Adam Davies.<br /> <br />Mord McGhee's unique brand of literature flies beneath the banner: "IT'S NOT DYSTOPIA TO THINK HISTORY WILL REPEAT ITSELF." He's a retired musician and his writing is a wild blend rock'n'roll, fantasy and science fiction. <br /><br />Mord McGhee has been writing professionally since March of 2014. Mord is a 2016 Silver Falchion Finalist and 2014 Dan Poynter's Science Fiction Medal-winner. He's from the land of Andy Warhol and Andrew Carnegie, Southwestern Pennsylvania. He loves to read. "The library," he says, "books... are our bastion of hope against dystopia." <br />McGhee's body of work spans anthologies, novels, and magazines worldwide. He's been fortunate to find kind words from an amazing group of colleagues, such as world's greatest cryptozoologist Loren Coleman, world renowned adventurer Adam Davies, Jack the Ripper casebook member and speaker, Robert E. Anderson, filmmaker George C. Romero (Cameron), and MEG mastermind, Steve Alten.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
